### Post by Gnusboy on 2014-11-22
I upgraded to 14.04 a few weeks ago and I am generally happy with it. However, I keeping being sent multiple software & updates almost daily even though I all I have signed up for are the
important security updates and the recommended updates. The update page is different from the one in 12.04 - it shows listings for Ubuntu software, other software, updates, authentication and additional drivers. It may have been somewhere in 12.04, but I don't recall seeing the same window as I get now. There are dozens of listings for just about every program installed in my current version.

When I used 12.04 I was always signed up for the Canonical supported free software "Main" and Canonical "Universe", the restricted Proprietary Drivers. But I seldom got more than the security updates.

Can I Stop this madness by unclicking the Canonical stuff, or do I really "need" to install al this other stuff?



.

### Post by vasa1 on 2014-11-22
If you think it's madness use some other distro or Windows or a Mac.

If you want help please be more explicit. Your needs may not be the same as someone else's.

Tell us what this "other stuff" is.

Put up your /etc/apt/sources.list.

### Post by grahammechanical on 2014-11-22
I think in 12.04 it was called Software Sources. The change of name to Software and Updates came more than a year ago and the only difference I notice is that the Additional Drivers utility is now a tab in Software and Updates instead of being a stand alone utility.

I do not understand the comment about "dozens of listing for just about every program installed." Are you referring to the tabs in Software and Updates or to the listing that we get when Software Updater shows us and describes what packages are available to be updated?

In 12.04 we got very little information about the packages that were being updated. Or to put it another way, information was not in a form that the ordinary person could understand. Well, at least I found it all rather incomprehensible. With Software Updater we get information about the packages that is much more descriptive. It helps me to understand what I am getting.

I use the development version and it does indeed get updates every day as the development branch is developed into the next Ubuntu release. But a released version of Ubuntu should not be getting updates every day. In fact a strict procedure is followed for what are called Stable Release Updates (SRU).

> [COLOR=#333333][FONT=Ubuntu Beta]Once an Ubuntu release has been completed and published, updates for it are only released under certain circumstances, and must follow a special procedure called a "stable release update" or SRU.[/FONT][/COLOR]

[https://wiki.ubuntu.com/StableReleaseUpdates](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/StableReleaseUpdates)

Here is a list of "proposed" updates to fix various bugs that are waiting to go in the "updates" channel. 

[http://people.canonical.com/~ubuntu-archive/pending-sru.html](http://people.canonical.com/~ubuntu-archive/pending-sru.html)

It is all part of the work of keeping our versions of Ubuntu secure. And if some vulnerability is found in some code that comes from other software projects and a fix is provided then it is important that the vulnerability be patched as soon as possible.

You will notice in Software Updater that some updates are listed but are not ticked for being updated. In that case those updates will appear every time we run Software Updater. What is happening here is called Phased Updates. It means that 10% of users will get the updates which will be held back to the other 90% of users. If the first 10% of people do not complain that something is wrong, then another 10% of users get the update. And so on until everyone gets the update. A bug fix may itself cause another bug. Phased Updates are an attempt to detect what are called regression bugs before every user receives the updates. This could be what you are seeing. That could make it seem that we are getting lots of updates every day. I will admit that.

[https://wiki.ubuntu.com/PhasedUpdates](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/PhasedUpdates)

Regards.

### Post by monkeybrain20122 on 2014-11-23
Did you add any ppa or enable 'proposed updates'? (you should disable 'proposed updates' if you have activated it. which is disabled by default)
I hardly get any update other than the ones from ppas that I added myself.

 In any case what is the problem? It is not like Windows that you have to restart the computer everytime you get updates. And even for kernel and driver updates that require restart to kick in you don't have to restart as long as you are not in a rush to experience the updates.

---

### Post by ian-weisser on 2014-11-23
220MB of updates seems unusual and does not match my experience.
Have you noticed any error messages?

Please open a terminal, and try the following two commands.
Please copy-and-paste the entire output here. It may be quite long.
```
sudo apt-get update
sudo apt-get --simulate upgrade
```

### Post by ian-weisser on 2014-12-07
> **Gnusboy said:**
> 
1) Are all updates officially sent by Ubuntu safe? 
2) Can they make my system unstable
3)  If I turnoff everything except the security updates, will it cause the  currently installed apps to stop functioning, or will they keep working  and just go out of date?

Thanks for the list.

Looking it over, it seems like a completely normal set of long-delayed upgrades.

Here's an example from your list:
```
Inst python3-apport [2.14.1-0ubuntu3.5] (2.14.1-0ubuntu3.6 Ubuntu:14.04/trusty-updates [all])
```
This means that the system wants to update the python3-apport package.
You currently have version 2.14.1-0ubuntu3.5 installed.
The system wants to update to version 2.14.1-0ubuntu3.6 in the trusty-updates repository.

I don't see any of the usual suspects for a broken package manager in the data you have provided: No non-Ubuntu software, no wrong repositories, no partial upgrades, no unresolved past errors.
Good results, in other words.

Answers to your specific questions:
1) All updates in the trusty-updates repository are supported by Ubuntu. They are tested. They are as safe as can be. I install them without hesitation.
2) Updates from trusty-updates is very unlikely to make your system unstable. They are tested. I install them without hesitation.
3) By 'turn off', let's assume you mean 'Uncheck the box for trusty-updates in System Settings --> Software & Updates --> Updates.' The applications will keep working. You will continue to receive security updates. You will no longer be prompted for other updates (mostly bugfixes).  It's entirely your choice.

My recommendation:
Let the system download and install ALL those updates once.
Then go to System Settings --> Software & Updates --> Updates. Try changing "When there are security updates" to "Download and install automatically"
If, after a few days, you are still prompted for too many updates, let us know in this thread and we can discuss the next step.

---
